## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: thermomechanical constitutive modeling (solid mechanics / materials science)
**Analysis**: The variables (stress sigma, strain epsilon, temperature T) indicate a constitutive law for a solid under mechanical loading with temperature-dependent stiffness, yielding, and/or hardening/softening. Common relationships include thermoelasticity (modulus and thermal strain depend on T) and empirical plasticity models where flow stress depends on both epsilon and T.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hooke’s law with temperature-dependent modulus: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (linear thermoelastic stiffness changing with temperature)
- Exponential modulus softening: sigma = c0 * exp(-c1 * T) * epsilon (stiffness decreases approximately exponentially with T)
- Thermoelastic stress with thermal strain offset: sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * (T - c2)) (accounts for free thermal expansion reducing mechanical strain)
- Polynomial nonlinear elasticity: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (finite-strain or nonlinear elastic response at moderate strains)
- Hyperelastic stiffening (exponential): sigma = c0 * (exp(c1 * epsilon) - 1) (rubbery/polymeric networks or large-strain stiffening)
- Hollomon/Ludwik-type hardening with temperature shift: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) + c2 * epsilon**c3 (flow stress = offset + power-law hardening, both can vary with T)
- Ramberg–Osgood-like explicit stress form: sigma = c0 * epsilon / (1 + c1 * epsilon**c2) (captures initial linearity with gradual hardening/curvature)
- Voce saturation hardening: sigma = c0 + c1 * (1 - exp(-c2 * epsilon)) (hardening that saturates at large strain)
- Temperature-softening multiplicative factor: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 - (c3 * (T - c4))**c5) (plastic flow stress reduced as T rises toward a reference)
- Coupled thermoelastic nonlinearity: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T + c2 * T**2) * (c3 * epsilon + c4 * epsilon**2) (separable temperature- and strain-nonlinear stiffness)
- Thermally activated-like softening without 1/T form: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * exp(-c3 * (T - c4)) (strength decays approximately exponentially with increasing T)
- Creep/viscoplastic effective relation (empirical, strain-only proxy): sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (when epsilon reflects accumulated inelastic strain correlated with T)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Small-strain linear elasticity → sigma proportional to epsilon, with slope identified as an effective modulus E(T) (i.e., sigma ≈ E(T) * epsilon).
- Thermal expansion effects → sigma depends on (epsilon - alpha*(T - T0)); this appears as an affine shift in epsilon by a T-dependent term.
- Thermal softening of stiffness or strength → multiplicative decreasing factors in T such as exp(-c*T) or (1 - (c*(T-T0))**m).
- Work/strain hardening → sigma increases sublinearly or superlinearly with epsilon via epsilon**n (n<1 concave, n>1 convex), often added to a base stress.
- Hardening saturation (dislocation storage/recovery balance) → sigma approaches an asymptote using 1 - exp(-c*epsilon) or similar saturating forms.
- Large-strain polymer/entropic stiffening → rapid growth with strain represented by exp(c*epsilon) or higher-order polynomial terms.
- Separable thermo-mechanical effects → sigma ≈ f(epsilon) * g(T) is common when temperature primarily scales strength/modulus rather than changing shape vs strain.
- Thermo-mechanical coupling beyond separability → cross-terms like T*epsilon or T*epsilon**2 indicate temperature changes the curvature/hardening rate, not just the overall scale.

**Candidate 23:** `T*c0*epsilon + c1*epsilon + c2*epsilon^c3 + c4*epsilon + c5*log(T*c6+1)*log(c7*epsilon+1) + c8*epsilon*exp(T*c9)`

This has epsilon^c3 (can be epsilon² if c3=2), log(T*c6+1)*log(c7*epsilon+1), and T*epsilon terms plus epsilon*exp(T*c9).

GT = 90.776*epsilon² + 2.482*T*log(epsilon+1) - 838.769*log(epsilon+1)

For the T*log(epsilon+1) term: we need something linear in T times log(epsilon+1). We have log(T*c6+1)*log(c7*epsilon+1) which is NOT linear in T. We also have c8*epsilon*exp(T*c9) - if c9=0, this becomes c8*epsilon. And T*c0*epsilon.

The problem is we can't get T*log(epsilon+1) from these terms. log(T*c6+1) ≈ T*c6 only for small T*c6, not exactly. **NO MATCH.**

Candidate 23 verdict: [NO MATCH]
